[6:0:191,286] 0750   Office of the Lieutenant Governor  

[7:0:66,307] Under California's Constitution, the Lieutenant Governor serves as Acting Governor whenever the Governor is absent from the  

[7:1:66,317] state, and automatically becomes Governor if a vacancy occurs in the Office of Governor. The Lieutenant Governor is also  

[7:2:66,328] President of the Senate and votes in case of a tie.  

[8:0:66,345] The Lieutenant Governor serves as a voting member of the Board of Regents of the University of California, the Board of  

[8:1:66,355] Trustees of the California State University system, and the Board of Governors of the California Community Colleges system.  

[8:2:66,366] The Lieutenant Governor also sits on the Calbright College Board of Trustees.  

[8:3:66,383] The Lieutenant Governor also serves on, and rotates with the State Controller, as chair of the three-member State Lands  

[8:4:66,394] Commission, which oversees the control and leasing of millions of acres of state-owned land, including offshore oil resources,  

[8:5:66,404] as well as use and permitting for all navigable waterways in California. The Commission also manages state land-use planning  

[8:6:66,414] and revenues, and related interstate issues. During alternate years, when the Lieutenant Governor serves as Chairperson of  

[8:7:66,424] the State Lands Commission, the Lieutenant Governor also serves as a member of the Ocean Protection Council   and as a  

[8:8:66,434] non-voting member of the California Coastal Commission.  

[9:0:66,452] In addition, under state statutes, the Lieutenant Governor chairs the California Commission for Economic Development, which  

[9:1:66,462] provides support and guidance to the Governor, Legislature, and private sector regarding the development of California's  

[9:2:66,472] economy.

[12:0:66,621] The constitutional office of the Attorney General, as chief law officer of the state, has the responsibility to see that the laws of  

[12:1:66,631] California are uniformly and adequately enforced. This responsibility is fulfilled through the diverse programs of the Department  

[12:2:66,641] of Justice.  

[13:0:66,661] The Department of Justice is responsible for providing skillful and efficient legal services on behalf of the people of California.  

[13:1:66,672] The Attorney General represents the people in all matters before the Appellate and Supreme Courts of California and the  

[13:2:66,682] United States; serves as legal counsel to state officers, boards, commissioners, and departments; represents the people in  

[13:3:66,692] actions to protect the environment and to enforce consumer, antitrust, and civil laws; and assists district attorneys in the  

[13:4:66,702] administration of justice. The Department provides oversight, enforcement, education, and regulation of California's firearms/ 

[13:5:66,712] dangerous weapon laws; provides evaluation and analysis of physical evidence; regulates legal gambling activities in

[10:0:66,466] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[10:1:65,485] • DNA Identification Fund Revenue Backfill—The Budget includes $16 million one-time ($6 million General Fund and $10  

[10:2:76,495] million Fingerprint Fees Account) to backfill declining fine and fee revenues in the DNA Identification Fund. This funding will  

[10:3:76,506] enable the Department of Justice to continue processing forensic evidence for client counties.  

[10:4:65,522] • Police Use of Force (Chapter 326, Statutes of 2020 (AB 1506))—The Budget includes $15.3 million General Fund in  

[10:5:76,532] 2021-22, increasing to $15.6 million ongoing, to establish four teams, two in the northern region of California, and two in the  

[10:6:76,542] southern region of California, to conduct independent investigations of officer involved shootings that result in the death of an  

[10:7:76,552] unarmed individual, and provide victim advocacy and supportive services to the survivors of those killed in officer-involved  

[10:8:76,563] shootings that are being investigated.  

[11:0:65,579] • Medi-Cal Fraud and Elder Abuse Workload—The Budget includes $13.9 million ongoing ($3.5 million False Claims Act Fund  

[11:1:76,589] and $10.4 million Federal Trust Fund) to allow full expenditure of a reoccurring federal grant that supports the Division’s  

[11:2:76,599] workload in eight regional offices.  

[12:0:65,615] • Gun Violence Reduction Grant Program—The Budget includes $10.3 million one-time General Fund to provide grants to  

[12:1:76,626] county sheriffs departments conducting activities related to the seizure of weapons and ammunition from persons who are  

[12:2:76,636] prohibited from possessing them.  

[13:0:65,652] • Retroactive Expungement of Arrest Records—The Budget includes $7.5 million one-time General Fund and statutory  

[13:1:76,662] changes to extend Chapter 578, Statutes of 2019 (AB 1076), which provides prospective arrest records relief for certain non-

[13:2:76,672] violent crimes, to retroactively provide such relief going back to 1973.  

[14:0:65,689] • Sexual Assault Kit Backlog for Local Law Enforcement Agencies—The Budget includes $4 million one-time General Fund for  

[14:1:76,699] grants to reduce local law enforcement agencies’ sexual assault kit backlog.

[5:0:66,293] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,313] 0435 - LEGAL SERVICES  

[7:0:66,333] Legal Services is organized into four elements: (1) Civil Law, (2) Criminal Law,   (3) Public Rights, and (4) Medi-Cal and Elder  

[7:1:66,343] Abuse.  

[8:0:66,364] Civil Law represents the State of California and its officers, agencies, departments, boards, commissions, and employees in  

[8:1:66,374] civil matters. It provides advice to these clients, defends cases brought against them, and prosecutes cases to vindicate state  

[8:2:66,384] interests. Deputy Attorneys General in Civil Law are responsible for managing and litigating cases before administrative  

[8:3:66,394] tribunals, and in both state and federal courts at the trial level and on appeal, including appeals before the United States and  

[8:4:66,404] California Supreme Courts. Deputies work in one of   nine sections: Business and Tax; Cannabis Control; Correctional Law;  

[8:5:66,415] Employment and Administrative Mandates; Government Law; Health, Education, and Welfare; Health Quality Enforcement;  

[8:6:66,425] Licensing; or Tort and Condemnation.  

[9:0:66,445] Criminal Law represents the   People of the State of California   in criminal matters before the Appellate and Supreme courts.  

[9:1:66,455] Criminal Law also fulfills the Attorney General's responsibilities of assisting district attorneys in cases for which they are  

[10:0:66,466] recused, conducting criminal investigations, representing the Governor, Board of Parole Hearings, and California Department of  

[10:1:66,476] Corrections and Rehabilitation in state and federal habeas corpus cases and appeals, and other proceedings relating to parole  

[10:2:66,486] decisions and conditions of confinement in the state prisons, and defending criminal judgements in state and federal habeas  

[10:3:66,496] corpus matters. Additional responsibilities include enforcing the Political Reform Act, advising the Governor on extradition  

[10:4:66,506] matters, and investigating, prosecuting, and coordinating litigation involving white-collar crimes, high-tech/computer/privacy  

[10:5:66,517] crimes, financial crimes, human trafficking, environmental crimes, and public corruption.  

[11:0:66,537] Public Rights protects and preserves the public’s interests by providing legal services to state agencies, boards and  

[12:0:66,547] commissions, and Constitutional Officers, and by bringing actions in the name of the Attorney General to protect the public.  

[12:1:66,557] Public Rights provides specialized services in the following areas: Civil Rights Enforcement (including the Bureau of Children's  

[12:2:66,568] Justice); Worker Rights and Fair Labor; Charitable Trusts Enforcement and Regulation (including the Registry of Charitable  

[12:3:66,578] Trusts); Natural Resources Law; Corporate Fraud (including False Claims, Energy and Corporate Responsibility); Healthcare  

[12:4:66,588] Rights and Access (including Tobacco Litigation and Enforcement, and Healthcare Competition and Pharmaceutical pricing);  

[12:5:66,598] Indian and Gaming Law; Environment Law (including the Bureau of Environmental Justice); Land Law; Consumer Protection  

[12:6:66,608] (including Privacy Enforcement); and Antitrust Law.  

[13:0:66,626] The Division of Medi-Cal Fraud and Elder Abuse represents the People of the State of California in both criminal and civil  

[13:1:66,636] matters involving Medi-Cal provider fraud and the abuse or neglect of elder and dependent adults living in residential facilities.  

[13:2:66,646] The Division is a vertical prosecution unit whose investigations are conducted by multidisciplinary teams consisting of Special  

[13:3:66,657] Agents, Investigative Auditors, and Deputy Attorneys General. Deputy Attorneys General from the Division represent the  

[13:4:66,667] People of the State of California in both federal and state courts. Types of cases frequently prosecuted by the Division include  

[13:5:66,677] fraud committed against the Medi-Cal program by doctors, pharmacies, clinics, dentists, medical equipment suppliers, hospice,  

[13:6:66,687] home health companies, and all other Medi-Cal providers; elder or dependent adult abuse or neglect in skilled nursing facilities,  

[13:7:66,697] residential care facilities for the elderly, intermediate care facilities for the developmentally disabled, and other specified  

[13:8:66,708] residential care facilities.  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] 2021-22 STATE BUDGET — LJE   150 

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:189,32] 0820   Department of Justice - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] 0440 - LAW ENFORCEMENT  

[4:0:66,89] The Division of Law Enforcement is organized into five areas: (1) Bureau of Firearms, (2) Bureau of Forensic Services, (3)  

[4:1:66,99] Bureau of Gambling Control, (4) Bureau of Investigation, and (5) the Office of the Chief.  

[5:0:66,120] The Bureau of Firearms provides oversight, enforcement, education, and regulation of California's firearms and  

[6:0:66,130] ammunitions   laws by administering a multitude of different state-mandated firearms and ammunition-related programs. It is  

[6:1:66,140] accomplished by conducting firearm and ammunition eligibility checks, conducting compliance inspections at firearm dealers,  

[6:2:66,150] ammunition vendors, and manufacturers, and by providing valuable training to stakeholders statewide. Special Agents conduct  

[6:3:66,160] investigations on armed and prohibited persons and other investigations resulting in the seizure of firearms, magazines, and  

[6:4:66,171] ammunition. Agents also conduct investigations to monitor and   prevent illegal   firearm trafficking at permitted gun shows in  

[6:5:66,181] accordance with state and federal laws.  

[7:0:66,201] The Bureau of Forensic Services (BFS) provides evaluation and analysis of physical evidence, crime scene investigation, and  

[7:1:66,211] expert court testimony to federal, state and local law enforcement agencies, district attorneys, and courts. The BFS operates 10  

[7:2:66,222] regional crime laboratories and two specialized laboratories, the Jan Bashinski DNA Laboratory and Statewide Toxicology  

[7:3:66,232] Laboratory, which   serve 46 of California’s 58 counties. The BFS also operates the California Criminalistics Institute forensic  

[7:4:66,242] training facility that provides training for forensic scientists worldwide. The BFS maintains the state DNA database, which stores  

[7:5:66,252] and regularly searches the DNA profiles of sex and violent offenders and felony arrestees against the DNA profiles of evidence  

[7:6:66,262] from unsolved crimes.  

[8:0:66,283] The Bureau of Gambling Control regulates legal gambling activities in California to ensure gambling is conducted honestly and  

[8:1:66,293] is free from criminal and corruptive elements. This is accomplished by investigating the qualifications of individuals and  

[8:2:66,303] business entities who apply for licenses and monitoring the conduct of these licensees to ensure compliance with the Gambling  

[8:3:66,313] Control Act and applicable regulations. The Bureau conducts criminal investigations in and around tribal casinos and California  

[8:4:66,324] cardrooms. In addition, the Bureau conducts audits and reviews for tribal gaming to ensure that each tribe is in compliance with  

[8:5:66,334] all aspects of the state gaming compact.  

[9:0:66,354] The Bureau of Investigation is the premiere investigative bureau that is responsible for investigating and dismantling criminal  

[9:1:66,364] organizations, as well as assisting with the prosecution of serious criminal offenses which present a significant and multi-

[9:2:66,375] jurisdictional threat to California. The Bureau prioritizes investigations related to transnational criminal organizations involved in  

[9:3:66,385] gangs, as well as cases involving   major white-collar fraud, underground economy, drug trafficking, recycle fraud, officer-

[9:4:66,395] involved shootings, homicides, foreign prosecution, human trafficking and sexual predator apprehension crimes. In addition, the  

[9:5:66,405] Bureau serves a principal role in providing leadership, coordination, and support to law enforcement through intelligence units  

[9:6:66,415] and multi-agency drug, gang and major crimes task forces statewide.  

[10:0:66,436] The Office of the Chief provides administrative support to the investigative, regulatory, and forensic components of the Division  

[10:1:66,446] of Law Enforcement and other criminal justice agencies. The Office serves as the policy-making and oversight body for its four  

[10:2:66,456] operational bureaus.  

[11:0:66,474] 0445 - CALIFORNIA JUSTICE INFORMATION SERVICES  

[12:0:66,494] The California Justice Information Services Division provides criminal justice intelligence, information, and identification  

[12:1:66,505] services to law enforcement, regulatory agencies, and the public. Four major functional areas carry out these primary services:  

[12:2:66,515] 1) The Justice Data and Investigative Services Bureau consolidates the identification, investigative, and field services functions,  

[12:3:66,525] providing information and technical assistance on manual and automated systems including the fingerprint identification system  

[12:4:66,535] and the violent crime information system; 2) The Bureau of Criminal Information and Analysis consolidates the functions related  

[12:5:66,545] to the authorization, release, and use of criminal offender record information for law enforcement investigatory and regulatory  

[12:6:66,556] purposes; 3) The Hawkins Data Center operates the Criminal Justice Information System and the California Law Enforcement  

[12:7:66,566] Telecommunications System, as well as provides IT services for the Attorney General’s Office; 4) the Operations Support  

[12:8:66,576] Program provides business resumption planning and administrative support and oversight; and 5) the Department of Justice  

[12:9:66,586] Research Center, within the Operations Support Program, oversees statistical models and engages in the analysis of data to  

[12:10:66,596] provide evidence-based research.  

[13:0:66,614] 9900 - DIRECTORATE AND ADMINISTRATION  

[14:0:66,632] The Directorate and the Administration Division of the Department of Justice consists of the Division of Operations and the  

[14:1:66,642] Attorney General's Executive Office. The Executive Office maintains the overall direction and administration of the diverse  

[14:2:66,652] programs and projects of the department, including the Equal Employment Rights and Resolution Office, the Office of Program  

[14:3:66,662] Oversight and Accountability, the Opinions Unit, the Solicitor General's Unit, the Office of Legislative Affairs, the Office of  

[14:4:66,673] Communications and the Public Inquiry Unit. In addition, the Division of Operations provides support functions essential to the  

[14:5:66,683] department's operations, including fiscal, personnel, and specialized business services such as legal secretarial support,  

[14:6:66,693] litigation support, legal case management services, and facilities management.  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[8:0:66,477] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[9:0:66,496] The Department of Justice (DOJ) has 96 facilities statewide totaling 1.8 million square feet, of which 14 facilities and 1.2 million  

[9:1:66,506] square feet are state-owned locations.   The remaining facilities are leased from non-state entities. 

[10:0:66,524] These facilities support the constitutional office of the Attorney General who, as Chief Law Enforcement Officer of the state, has  

[10:1:66,534] the responsibility to see that the laws of California are uniformly and adequately enforced. This responsibility is fulfilled through  

[10:2:66,544] the diverse legal, law enforcement and criminal justice information programs of the DOJ.  

[11:0:242,580] 0840   State Controller  

[12:0:66,601] The State Controller is the chief fiscal officer of California, the fifth largest economy in the world. Principally responsible for  

[12:1:66,612] transparency and accountability of the state's financial resources, the Controller ensures the appropriate disbursement and  

[12:2:66,622] tracking of taxpayer dollars. The Controller serves on dozens of state boards, commissions, and committees with  

[12:3:66,632] duties   ranging from   administrative oversight of the nation's two largest public pension funds,   to protection of state lands and  

[12:4:66,642] coastlines,   to modernization and financing of major infrastructure. The Controller also offers fiscal guidance to local  

[12:5:66,652] governments and has independent auditing authority over government agencies related to the spending of state funds. The  

[12:6:66,663] Controller's primary objectives are to:  

[13:0:65,680] • Account for and control disbursement of all state funds, issuing warrants in payment of the state's bills, including lottery  

[13:1:76,691] prizes.  

[14:0:65,707] • Determine legality and accuracy of financial claims against the state.  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[7:0:66,478] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[7:1:66,498] 0500100 - ACCOUNTING AND REPORTING  

[8:0:66,518] The State Accounting and Reporting Division maintains uniform and systematic control accounts of all receipts, payments,  

[8:1:66,528] appropriations, state fund balances, and bonded indebtedness; monitors the cash flow of the General Fund; administers the  

[8:2:66,538] statewide discharge from accountability program; participates in offsetting monies owed to the state; reports the financial  

[8:3:66,549] condition of the state; and collaborates with the Department of Finance, the Treasurer, and the Department of General Services  

[8:4:66,559] to develop and implement the Financial Information System for California (FI$Cal) to ensure the system meets the state's  

[8:5:66,569] primary objectives and provides best business practices for the state.  

[9:0:66,589] The Local Government Programs and Services Division maintains a database of information and reports on local financial  

[9:1:66,600] transactions and government compensation; apportions shared revenues to local governments; administers local mandated  

[9:2:66,610] cost programs; approves county cost allocation plans; prescribes uniform accounting procedures for counties, special districts,  

[9:3:66,620] and trial court revenues; administers and collects estate and inheritance taxes; collects delinquent insurance and motor vehicle  

[9:4:66,630] fuel taxes, petroleum and gas assessments, and trial court penalties; refunds gasoline taxes paid on fuel consumed for off-

[9:5:66,640] highway purposes; instructs and advises county tax collectors; approves state and local government requests to participate in  

[9:6:66,651] the Interagency Intercept Collection Program; and administers the Property Tax Postponement Program for seniors and people  

[9:7:66,661] with disabilities.  

[9:8:66,678] 0500200 - AUDITS  

[10:0:66,699] The Audits Division determines the legality and accuracy of all claims against the state through the performance of prepayment  

[10:1:66,709] audits; assures the accuracy of local government claims and financial statements submitted to the state and federal  

[11:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,69] governments by establishing and updating audit guidelines, and reviewing audits performed by independent auditors; performs

[3:2:66,89] that receive pass-through federal funds from state agencies; and audits major businesses for compliance with the Unclaimed  

[3:3:66,99] Property Law.  

[4:0:66,117] 0500300 - PERSONNEL AND PAYROLL SERVICES  

[5:0:66,137] The Personnel and Payroll Services Division administers the state's payroll, employment history, the automated travel expense  

[5:1:66,148] reimbursement system, and leave accounting processes. The Division works with the Department of Human Resources,  

[5:2:66,158] California Public Employees' Retirement System, Judicial Council, Department of Finance, and California State University  

[5:3:66,168] Chancellor's Office to maximize the efficiency of the state's personnel and payroll functions.  

[6:0:66,188] The California State Payroll System Project was initiated to modernize the statewide human resource management and  

[6:1:66,199] payroll   systems as part of a fully integrated solution. The system should enable the state to improve management processes  

[6:2:66,209] and fulfill its payroll, reporting, and deduction processing obligations accurately and on time.  

[6:3:66,226] 0500400 - UNCLAIMED PROPERTY  

[7:0:66,247] The Unclaimed Property Division administers the Unclaimed Property Law by providing one central source for owners to claim  

[7:1:66,257] their property; notifying owners of their unclaimed property before it is transferred to the state; receiving unclaimed property  

[7:2:66,267] from banks, savings and loans, insurance companies, and other businesses; and providing outreach and education for  

[7:3:66,277] businesses holding unclaimed property. 

[7:4:66,295] 0500500 - DISBURSEMENTS  

[8:0:66,316] The Disbursements Bureau produces and delivers all payments of the state's obligations after auditing and clearance through  

[8:1:66,326] control accounts.   Examples of some of the state's payments are personal income tax refunds, payroll, vendor payments,   and  

[8:2:66,336] retirement payments. Disbursements also provides post-issuance services including disposition of undeliverable warrants; lost  

[8:3:66,346] warrant duplication; and maintenance and production of paid warrant images.  

[8:4:66,364] 0500900 - DEPARTMENTAL ADMINISTRATION  

[9:0:66,384] The Executive Office and the Administration Program provide executive direction and support services to all   divisions in the  

[9:1:66,394] State Controller's Office. The Information Systems Division (ISD)   develops, maintains, and operates all of the department's  

[9:2:66,405] mainframe, client-server, and web-based systems; and oversees the planning, procurement, use, and maintenance of  

[9:3:66,415] information technology hardware and software. Within ISD, the Information Security Office evaluates security compliance,  

[9:4:66,425] internal control management, and security governance.

[8:0:216,349] 0845   Department of Insurance  

[9:0:66,371] California's publicly-elected Insurance Commissioner regulates the fourth largest insurance economy in the world with  

[9:1:66,381] insurance companies collecting more than $340 billion in premiums annually in California while protecting consumers and  

[9:2:66,391] ensuring the health and competitiveness of the insurance marketplace. The vision of the California Department of Insurance  

[9:3:66,401] (CDI) is "Insurance Protection for All Californians." CDI accomplishes this by enforcing insurance laws and regulations,  

[9:4:66,412] assisting consumers in their dealings with insurance companies, and using innovation to improve services for insurance  

[9:5:66,422] producers, consumers, and businesses.  

[10:0:66,439] CDI licenses and regulates insurance companies, and individuals in California. Currently, CDI oversees and licenses  

[10:1:66,450] approximately 1,400 insurance companies and approximately 425,000 individuals and business entities as insurance agents,  

[10:2:66,460] brokers, adjusters, and bail agents. Additionally, CDI receives and investigates approximately 200,000 consumer inquiries and  

[10:3:66,470] complaints annually, performs ongoing risk-focused financial surveillance of insurance companies, receives more than 23,000  

[10:4:66,480] suspected fraudulent claim referrals annually and investigates approximately 1,300 of those referrals, receives and reviews  

[10:5:66,490] approximately 6,200 rate filing applications annually, and, works in conjunction with local, state, and federal law enforcement  

[10:6:66,501] agencies to investigate and prosecute fraudulent insurance practices.

[18:0:66,711] 0520 - REGULATION OF INSURANCE COMPANIES AND INSURANCE PRODUCERS

[0:0:66,13] 2021-22 STATE BUDGET — LJE   184 

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:181,32] 0845   Department of Insurance - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The objectives of this program are to: (1) oversee the financial solvency of insurance companies to ensure   they can provide the  

[3:1:66,79] benefits and protections promised to California policyholders; (2) review complex, principles-based reserving methods and  

[3:2:66,89] underlying assumptions to avoid reliance on “black box” models; (3) prevent unlawful or unfair practices by insurance  

[3:3:66,99] companies and insurance producers as defined by the Insurance Code; (4) ensure that property and casualty insurance rates  

[3:4:66,109] are not excessive, inadequate, unfairly discriminatory, or otherwise in violation of the Insurance Code and the California Code  

[3:5:66,120] of Regulations; (5) assess and implement strategies to reduce climate risk impacts in the insurance sector; (6) review health  

[3:6:66,130] insurance rates filed with CDI to determine whether they are reasonable and work with insurance companies to get  

[3:7:66,140] unreasonable rates lowered; (7) review long term care insurance rates to ensure requested rate increases are actuarially  

[3:8:66,150] justified and not excessive; (8) ensure that applicants for insurance licenses, and holders of insurance licenses, satisfy and  

[3:9:66,160] maintain the qualifications for licensure. Additionally, CDI administers the estates of insolvent and delinquent insurance  

[3:10:66,171] companies through the Conservation and Liquidation Office.  

[3:11:66,188] 0525 - CONSUMER PROTECTION  

[4:0:66,209] The objectives of this program are to: (1) provide direct service to California consumers by protecting insurance policyholders  

[4:1:66,219] and other parties involved in insurance transactions against unfair or illegal practices with respect to claims handling, rating, or  

[4:2:66,229] underwriting by insurers; (2) protect applicants and policyholders from discriminatory, unlawful, or fraudulent practices or  

[4:3:66,239] incompetence relating to the sale of insurance; (3) oversee programs that benefit California's underserved communities and (4)  

[4:4:66,250] assist wildfire survivors, local governments, small businesses, community service organizations, and neighborhood  

[4:5:66,260] associations by providing access to CDI’s services through electronic and printed informational guides, workshops, seminars,  

[4:6:66,270] roundtables and town halls.  

[4:7:66,288] 0530 - FRAUD CONTROL  

[5:0:66,305] The objective of this program is to protect the public from economic loss by actively investigating, arresting and referring for  

[5:1:66,316] prosecution those who commit insurance fraud and other violations of the law. The program is primarily staffed by sworn peace  

[5:2:66,326] officers who conduct criminal investigations of insurance fraud and related criminal cases. The program administers the  

[5:3:66,336] Insurance Frauds Prevention Act (IFPA), which authorizes CDI to conduct criminal insurance fraud investigations. In addition,  

[5:4:66,346] the IFPA authorizes the Commissioner to initiate or intervene in whistle-blower "qui tam" actions seeking civil penalties against  

[5:5:66,356] perpetrators of insurance fraud.  

[6:0:66,374] 0535 - GENERAL FUND TAX COLLECTION AND COMPLIANCE  

[7:0:66,392] This program performs tax collection, ensures the compliance of insurance companies and surplus line brokers with the laws  

[7:1:66,402] contained in the Insurance Code and Revenue and Taxation Code, and works with the California Department of Tax and Fee  

[7:2:66,412] Administration and the State Controller's Office on various refund, assessment, and accounting matters relative to the premium  

[7:3:66,422] tax program. Tax collections from this program are deposited in the state's General Fund.

[6:0:183,281] 0850   California State Lottery Commission  

[7:0:66,303] In 1984, Proposition 37 amended the California Constitution to authorize the establishment of a statewide lottery. As an  

[7:1:66,313] initiative statute, the California State Lottery Act (Act) of 1984 created the California State Lottery Commission and gave it  

[7:2:66,323] broad powers to oversee the operations of a statewide lottery. The purpose of the Act was to provide supplemental monies to  

[7:3:66,333] benefit public education. The Lottery is overseen by a five-person Commission appointed by the Governor and confirmed by  

[7:4:66,343] the State Senate.  

[8:0:66,361] The Act initially required that 50 percent of total annual revenues be returned to the public in the form of prizes and at least 34  

[8:1:66,371] percent of total revenues be allocated to the benefit of public education. No more than 16 percent of total revenues were to be  

[8:2:66,382] used for administrative costs.  

[9:0:66,399] In 2010, the Act was changed to allow the Lottery flexibility to pay out more money in prizes and reduce the administrative cost  

[9:1:66,409] limit to 13 percent of total revenues. Along with that flexibility, the new law requires the Lottery to meet minimum levels of  

[9:2:66,420] contribution to public education. Revenues to education are placed in a special fund, known as the California State Lottery  

[9:3:66,430] Education Fund, which holds revenues until they are allocated on a per capita basis, using prior year certified Average Daily  

[9:4:66,440] Attendance data, to the following categories: K-12 education, Community Colleges, the California State University, the  

[9:5:66,450] University of California, and other educational entities, including the California Schools for the Deaf and Blind.  

[9:6:66,468] In the 35 years since sales began in October 1985 through June 30, 2020, the California State Lottery has raised $37.6 billion  

[9:7:66,478] for public education, including approximately $1.5 billion in FY 2019-20.  

[10:0:66,496] Because of the inherently variable nature of lottery ticket sales, revenue estimates for 2020-21 and 2021-22 cannot be made  

[10:1:66,506] with certainty.

[12:0:66,573] Government Code, Title 2, Division 1, Chapter 12.5 (Sections 8880-8880.72).

[1:0:169,66] 0855   California Gambling Control Commission  

[2:0:66,87] The mission of the California Gambling Control Commission (Commission) is to protect the public by ensuring integrity and  

[2:1:66,97] justice in California's controlled gambling industry through effective regulations and fair application of the law. The Commission  

[2:2:66,108] has jurisdiction over gambling establishments (cardrooms), third-party providers of proposition player services, and certain  

[2:3:66,118] aspects of Tribal casinos, pursuant to its authority under state law and Tribal-State Gaming Compacts (Compacts). The  

[2:4:66,128] Commission also has jurisdiction over gaming policies, regulations, criteria, and standards.  

[3:0:66,146] There are 86 licensed cardrooms in California over which the Commission has broad regulatory and adjudicatory authority. This  

[3:1:66,156] authority extends to the operation, concentration, and supervision of the cardrooms and all persons and things related to each  

[3:2:66,166] licensed establishment.  

[4:0:66,184] The Commission has fiduciary, regulatory, and administrative responsibilities related to Tribal gaming that include: (1)  

[4:1:66,194] distributing specified Tribal gaming revenues to Non-Compact, Non-Gaming and Limited-Gaming Tribes; (2) making suitability  

[4:2:66,204] determinations for key employees, gaming resource suppliers, and financial sources; and (3) serving as the administrator of the  

[4:3:66,214] Indian Gaming Revenue Sharing Trust Fund, Indian Gaming Special Distribution Fund, and the Tribal Nation Grant Fund.

[5:0:66,180] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,199] 0570025 - COUNTY ASSESSMENT STANDARDS PROGRAM  

[6:0:66,217] This program ensures that taxable properties are enrolled and assessed by the 58 county assessors in full conformity with the  

[6:1:66,227] law. The BOE is also charged with providing consultation and services to the county assessors and their staff, establishing  

[6:2:66,237] standards, providing training for assessors and assessment appeals boards, evaluating the effectiveness of each county  

[6:3:66,247] assessor's administration, co-administering the welfare exemption, and administering the Legal Entity Ownership Program.  

[6:4:66,265] 0570050 - STATE-ASSESSED PROPERTY PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,286] This program   values and assesses   inter-county pipelines and properties owned or used by railroads, regulated telephone  

[7:1:66,296] companies, companies transmitting or selling gas or electricity, and private railroad car companies. Local jurisdictions use the  

[7:2:66,306] established values for the levy and collection of local property taxes. In addition, the BOE collects the Private Railroad Car Tax  

[7:3:66,316] that is deposited in the state General Fund.  

[7:4:66,334] 0570150 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE TAX PROGRAM  

[8:0:66,354] This program collects the excise tax imposed on the sale, distribution, or importation of alcoholic beverages in California. The  

[8:1:66,364] BOE contracts with the CDTFA to administer this program.  

[8:2:66,382] 0570575 - INSURANCE TAX PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,403] This program provides revenue to the Insurance Tax Fund. Revenue is generated from taxes assessed on insurance  

[9:1:66,413] premiums, underwriting profits from ocean marine insurance, and retaliatory assessments levied on   out-of-state insurers. The  

[9:2:66,423] taxes collected are used to pay refunds or transferred to the General Fund. The BOE contracts with the CDTFA to administer  

[9:3:66,433] this program.

[1:0:226,69] 0870   Office of Tax Appeals  

[2:0:66,91] The Office of Tax Appeals (OTA) was established effective January 1, 2018, by Chapter 16, Statutes of 2017 (AB 102). The  

[2:1:66,101] OTA performs those tax appeal duties formerly assigned by statute to the State Board of Equalization, including personal  

[2:2:66,111] income tax appeals, franchise tax appeals, and sales and use tax appeals. The OTA's mission is to ensure tax appeals are  

[2:3:66,121] performed in a fair, transparent, consistent, equitable, and impartial manner.  

[3:0:66,142] The OTA has hearing offices in Sacramento, Fresno, and Los Angeles.

[5:0:236,166] 0890   Secretary of State  

[6:0:66,188] The Secretary of State, a constitutionally established office, is the chief elections officer of the state and is responsible for the  

[6:1:66,198] administration and enforcement of election laws. The Office also is responsible for administering and enforcing laws pertaining  

[6:2:66,208] to filing documents associated with corporations, limited liability companies, partnerships, limited partnerships, unincorporated  

[6:3:66,218] associations and pertaining to filing bonds and perfecting security agreements. In addition, the Office is responsible for  

[6:4:66,229] commissioning notaries public, enforcing the notary laws, and in conjunction with being the home of the State Archives,  

[7:0:66,239] administering a state records management program and preserving documents and records having historical significance. The  

[7:1:66,249] Secretary of State is the filing officer for lobbying and campaign registration and disclosure documents filed under the Political  

[7:2:66,259] Reform Act. The Secretary of State also operates the Safe at Home program, maintains the Domestic Partners and Advance  

[7:3:66,269] Health Care Directives registries, provides support functions for the Voting Modernization Board, and is home to the California  

[7:4:66,280] Museum.  

[8:0:66,300] Policy associated with the administration of the Office is accomplished through the divisions of Elections, Political Reform,  

[8:1:66,310] Business Programs, Archives, Information Technology, and Management Services.

[12:0:66,492] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[13:0:65,511] •  Voter’s Choice Act— The Budget includes $5.8 million one-time General Fund to support voter education and outreach  

[13:1:76,522] initiatives in preparation for the 2022 Primary Election and General Election. This funding will be used to provide local  

[13:2:76,532] assistance to counties adopting the Voter’s Choice Act elections model and to fund statutory elections research and  

[13:3:76,542] reporting requirements.  

[14:0:65,558] •  Cal-ACCESS Replacement System Project— The Budget includes $10.7 million ($10.2 million General Fund and $500,000  

[14:1:76,568] Political Disclosure, Accountability, Transparency, and Access Fund) in 2021-22, decreasing to $5.4 million ongoing ($4.9  

[14:2:76,579] million General Fund and $500,000 Political Disclosure, Accountability, Transparency, and Access Fund), to support the  

[14:3:76,589] replacement of the Cal-ACCESS system.  

[15:0:65,605] •  Increasing Access to California’s Historic Records— The Budget includes $3.2 million General Fund in 2021-22, and  

[15:1:76,615] $1.6 million annually thereafter, to automate paper-based processes and support increased online and contactless access to  

[15:2:76,625] the State’s historic public records and data held in the State Archives.  

[16:0:65,642] •  Oral History and Digital Preservation Subscription— The Budget transfers $225,000 ongoing General Fund from the  

[16:1:76,652] State Library to the Secretary of State for the State Government Oral History Program and digital preservation subscription  

[16:2:76,662] services.  

[17:0:65,678] •  Help America Vote Act— The Budget includes $32.5 million one-time Federal Trust Fund to continue implementation of  

[17:1:76,688] statewide mandates of the Help America Vote Act of 2002 and pay for costs associated with the VoteCal statewide voter  

[17:2:76,699] registration system.

[8:0:66,653] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[8:1:66,672] 0700 - FILINGS AND REGISTRATIONS  

[9:0:66,692] The Business Programs Division is comprised of three primary areas: Business Entities, Uniform Commercial Code, and  

[9:1:66,702] Notary Public and Special Filings.  

[10:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 207 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:410,13] 2021-22 STATE BUDGET — LJE   205 

[2:0:201,32] 0890   Secretary of State - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] Business Entities examines, files, and maintains formation documents for new California business entities and qualifies out-of-

[3:1:66,79] state and international entities to conduct business in California; and also examines, files and maintains changes to the records  

[3:2:66,89] of domestic or qualified foreign business entities to ensure the business entities are properly formed, merged, converted,  

[3:3:66,99] amended, and dissolved in compliance with California law. Statements of Information containing key officers and contact  

[3:4:66,109] information are also processed and maintained for public and governmental use.  

[4:0:66,130] Uniform Commercial Code files certain financing statements allowing lending institutions to protect their financial interest in  

[4:1:66,140] personal property and established priority in case of debtor default or bankruptcy. Notices of judgment liens, attachment liens,  

[4:2:66,150] agricultural liens, and equipment liens are also filed in Uniform Commercial Code, as well as notices of various tax liens  

[4:3:66,160] submitted by state and federal taxing agencies such as the Franchise Tax Board and the Internal Revenue Service.  

[5:0:66,181] Notary Public and Special Filings appoints and commissions qualified notaries public for four- year terms, reviews and  

[6:0:66,191] approves notary public education courses, and certifies to the authenticity of signatures of notaries public and public officials on  

[6:1:66,201] documents for use in foreign countries. Special Filings include trademarks and service marks as well as surety bonds that  

[6:2:66,211] certain business entities are required to file, notices of joint power agreements, city and county charters, and claims for  

[6:3:66,222] successor-in-interest. This area also has disciplinary functions with regard to notaries public and immigration consultants.  

[7:0:66,242] The Advance Health Care Directive (AHCD) Registry maintains AHCDs, which allow a person to indicate his/her medical  

[7:1:66,252] treatment preferences if he/she cannot speak or make decisions for him/herself. The AHCD also may designate someone else  

[7:2:66,262] to make decisions regarding medical treatment. AHCDs and related information can be provided upon request to the  

[7:3:66,273] registrant's health care provider, public guardian, or legal representative.  

[8:0:66,293] The Domestic Partners Registry registers same-sex couples regardless of the age of the partners, and opposite-sex couples in  

[8:1:66,303] which one partner is at least 62 years old, as domestic partners in California.  

[9:0:66,324] The Victims of Corporate Fraud Compensation Fund provides limited restitution to victims of corporate fraud who are unable to  

[9:1:66,334] collect through other means on a judgment against a corporation for corporate fraud.  

[10:0:66,352] Safe at Home is a confidential mail forwarding program designed to assist victims and survivors of domestic violence and  

[10:1:66,362] human trafficking, sexual assault, stalking, elder/dependent adult abuse, their household members and minor children, and  

[10:2:66,372] reproductive healthcare employees, patients, and volunteers. Participants in the Safe at Home program are provided with a  

[10:3:66,382] free post office box to use as a substitute mailing address, thereby reducing or eliminating the need to use their actual  

[10:4:66,392] residential address. Once enrolled into the program, Safe at Home serves as a liaison for those participants who qualify for  

[10:5:66,403] additional confidential services offered by various state and local agencies.  

[11:0:66,420] 0705 - ELECTIONS  

[12:0:66,441] The Secretary of State serves as California’s chief elections officer and has broad responsibility to administer and oversee  

[12:1:66,451] federal and state elections held within California. The Elections Program maintains the official statewide database of registered  

[12:2:66,461] voters, tracks and certifies ballot measures, certifies candidates for placement on the ballot, and certifies official election  

[12:3:66,471] results. In addition, the program oversees the certification and modernization of voting equipment and the enhancement of  

[12:4:66,481] election processes. The program works to increase accessibility to voters, provides resources to educate voters on the  

[12:5:66,492] electoral system, and investigates election related criminal violations as provided by the California Elections Code.  

[13:0:66,512] This program includes the campaign and lobbying registration and disclosure provisions of the Political Reform Act of 1974.  

[13:1:66,522] Under this law, the Office registers all levels of campaign committees, and reviews for compliance with statutory requirements  

[13:2:66,532] all state-level candidate and campaign recipient committees, major donors, slate mailer, political party, and independent  

[13:3:66,543] expenditure committees. The program registers lobbyists (including placement agents), lobbying firms and lobbyist employers,  

[13:4:66,553] reviews for compliance with statutory requirements the periodic financial disclosure reports filed by lobbying entities, and  

[13:5:66,563] publishes a Lobbying Directory on the Internet. This program also supports the electronic filing requirements of the Political  

[13:6:66,573] Reform Act and posts relevant registration and disclosure information to the Office's web site so the public can track where  

[13:7:66,583] campaign money is raised and spent and what lobbying activity is occurring in state government. A searchable database of  

[13:8:66,594] campaign and lobbying financial activity is also provided through the web site.  

[14:0:66,611] 0710 - ARCHIVES  

[15:0:66,629] The California State Archives establishes and administers a records management program that applies efficient and  

[15:1:66,639] economical management methods to the creation, utilization, maintenance, retention, preservation, and disposal of state  

[15:2:66,649] records and acquires, indexes, preserves, and provides reference access to irreplaceable historic materials from the three  

[15:3:66,660] branches of state government. The Archives acquires physical and electronic records with legal, administrative or evidentiary  

[15:4:66,670] value, or that have historical significance. Materials are transferred to the Archives for permanent preservation.  

[16:0:66,688] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[17:0:66,708] This program develops and manages overall policy. It serves as the liaison to other state agencies, the Legislature, the federal  

[18:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,69] government, and other states' Secretaries of State. This program responds to constituent correspondence and requests from

[7:0:243,313] 0950   State Treasurer  

[7:1:66,335] The State Treasurer, a constitutionally established office, provides banking services for state government with goals to  

[7:2:66,345] minimize interest and service costs and to maximize yield on investments. The Treasurer is responsible for the custody of all  

[7:3:66,355] monies and securities belonging to or held in trust by the state; investment of temporarily idle state monies; administration of  

[7:4:66,365] the sale of state bonds, their redemption and interest payments; and payment of warrants or checks drawn by the State  

[7:5:66,376] Controller and other state agencies.

[8:0:66,354] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[8:1:66,373] 0740010 - INVESTMENT SERVICES  

[9:0:66,393] The Investment Division is responsible for investment of state monies from the date of receipt through the date of redemption.  

[9:1:66,404] During the 2019-20 fiscal year, this Division handled 8,964 security investment transactions totaling $415.4 billion. The Pooled  

[9:2:66,414] Money Investment Board (PMIB) program accounted for 7,687 of these transactions totaling $383.5 billion; time deposits  

[9:3:66,424] accounted for 1,002 transactions totaling $27.1 billion. The remaining $4.8 billion is invested on behalf of the state's special  

[9:4:66,434] funds, such as those associated with the California Housing Finance Agency, the Department of Fish and Wildlife, the state's  

[9:5:66,444] retirement system, etc. The Division also administers the Local Agency Investment Fund (LAIF), a voluntary investment  

[9:6:66,455] program created to offer California local agencies greater access to the financial markets through the PMIB program. In the  

[9:7:66,465] 2019-20 fiscal year, 2,362 local agencies participated in LAIF, with deposits averaging $27.3 billion for the fiscal year.  

[9:8:66,482] 0740019 - CENTRALIZED TREASURY AND SECURITIES MANAGEMENT  

[10:0:66,500] In 1949, the California Legislature amended Government Code Section 16305 to create the Centralized Treasury System  

[10:1:66,510] (CTS) thereby requiring agencies of the State to deposit their money in trust with the Treasurer. The legislation also requires  

[10:2:66,521] the Treasurer to safeguard the money and make safe and prudent investments. In 1955, the Legislature created the PMIB,  

[10:3:66,531] giving the Board the responsibility to designate the amount of money available for the investment in securities, bank deposits,  

[10:4:66,541] and loans to the General Fund.  

[11:0:66,559] The Centralized Treasury and Securities Management Division (CTSMD) oversees all banking aspects of the CTS. The goal of  

[11:1:66,569] the CTSMD is to maximize the earning of interest consistent with safe and prudent treasury management, and to ensure that  

[11:2:66,579] the depository banks provide the state with proper and adequate security for the deposit of state monies. The Treasurer  

[11:3:66,589] maintains demand bank accounts with eight banks for the purpose of providing necessary statewide depository coverage for  

[11:4:66,599] the remittance of funds collected by the various state agencies.  

[12:0:66,617] The CTSMD 1) monitors the cash flow of all state funds, forecasts cash balances, revenue, expenditures, and the amounts  

[12:1:66,627] available for daily investments, 2) ensures accurate and timely agency deposits, 3) administers and executes the wire transfer  

[12:2:66,638] of funds, 4) reconciles state accounts with depository banks and redeems all state items submitted by presenting banks for  

[12:3:66,648] payments, 5) executes the clearance and income collection for state investments (excluding PERS and STRS) and securities  

[12:4:66,658] pledged to the state, 6) fulfills the clearance and settlement of securities pledged to the state for the time, demand, and other  

[12:5:66,668] state agency programs, and 7) is responsible for the safekeeping of securities and other personal property owned by or  

[12:6:66,678] pledged to the state.  

[13:0:66,696] 0740028 - PUBLIC FINANCE

[2:0:208,32] 0950   State Treasurer - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The Public Finance Division is responsible for selling State of California general obligation bonds, commercial paper notes,  

[3:1:66,79] revenue anticipation notes, lease revenue bonds, revenue bonds, and any other indebtedness for all state agencies. The  

[3:2:66,89] Division provides debt administration services for most state bonds and is responsible for disseminating information to  

[3:3:66,99] bondholders through the Investor Relations Program.  

[4:0:66,120] The Division also assures compliance with federal tax laws applicable to certain state debt so there is no adverse  

[4:1:66,130] consequences to bondholders or increased borrowing costs to the state. The post-issuance tax compliance   includes monitoring  

[4:2:66,140] the use of bond proceeds, managing rebate and yield restriction compliance, coordinating necessary financial disclosure, and  

[4:3:66,150] ensuring proper record keeping.  

[5:0:66,168] 0740035 - ADMINISTRATION AND INFORMATION SERVICES  

[6:0:66,186] The Administration Division, Executive Office, and the Information Services Division provide executive direction and support  

[6:1:66,196] services to programs in the State Treasurer's Office. Services include budgeting, personnel, accounting, information systems,  

[6:2:66,206] business services, technical support, and production operations.

[8:0:66,456] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:0:66,476] 0780 - GOLDEN STATE SCHOLARSHARE COLLEGE SAVINGS TRUST PROGRAM  

[9:1:66,493] The Golden State ScholarShare College Savings Trust Program is California's state-sponsored 529 college savings plan  

[9:2:66,504] established to help families save for higher education.   Earnings are tax-free when used for qualified higher education expenses  

[9:3:66,514] (such as tuition, fees, supplies, books, computer equipment, and certain room and board expenses) at eligible educational  

[9:4:66,524] institutions.  

[9:5:66,542] 0785 - GOVERNOR'S SCHOLARSHIP PROGRAMS  

[10:0:66,559] The Governor's Scholarship Programs (GSP) rewarded public school students who demonstrated high academic achievement  

[10:1:66,570] with scholarships.   Students may have earned multiple $1,000 Governor's Scholars Awards and a one-time $2,500 Governor's  

[10:2:66,580] Distinguished Mathematics and Science Scholars Award for scores attained on tests taken in 2000, 2001, and 2002. GSP  

[10:3:66,590] became inoperative and was repealed after 2002.   The ScholarShare Investment Board administered scholarship awards that  

[10:4:66,600] were already earned until December 2019, when all students reached the age of 30 and all remaining scholarship awards were  

[10:5:66,610] subsequently reverted to the State General Fund.  

[10:6:66,628] 0790 - CALIFORNIA MEMORIAL SCHOLARSHIP PROGRAM  

[11:0:66,646] The California Memorial Scholarship Program provides scholarships to surviving dependents of California residents killed as a  

[11:1:66,656] result of the terrorist attacks of September 11, 2001.  

[11:2:66,674] 0795 - CALIFORNIA KIDS INVESTMENT AND DEVELOPMENT SAVINGS PROGRAM  

[11:3:66,691] The California Kids Investment and Development Savings Program (CalKIDS Program) provides California children born on or  

[11:4:66,702] after July 1, 2020 with college savings accounts, including seed deposits and potential incentives.  

[12:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[11:0:134,481] 0956   California Debt and Investment Advisory Commission  

[11:1:66,502] The mission of the California Debt and Investment Advisory Commission is to support and improve the practice of public  

[11:2:66,512] finance in California by providing responsive and reliable information, analysis, and training. The Commission assists California  

[11:3:66,523] state and local governments to monitor, issue, and manage public debt and to safely and prudently invest public funds.  

[12:0:66,543] The Commission consists of nine members including the State Treasurer, who serves as chairperson; the Governor or, upon  

[12:1:66,553] his designation, the Director of Finance; the State Controller; two local government finance officers appointed by the State  

[12:2:66,563] Treasurer; two members of the Assembly appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly; and two members of the Senate  

[12:3:66,574] appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules.

[9:1:66,434] 0800 - CALIFORNIA DEBT AND INVESTMENT ADVISORY COMMISSION  

[10:0:66,455] The Commission's primary objective is to enhance the knowledge of public officials with respect to the administration and  

[10:1:66,465] issuance of public debt and the investment of public funds. The Commission achieves this objective by performing functions in  

[10:2:66,475] three principal areas, including:  

[11:0:65,493] • Data Collection and Analysis - Serves as a clearinghouse of debt issued by California public entities and nonprofit student  

[11:1:76,503] loan corporations.  

[12:0:65,519] • Continuing Education - Provides educational seminars, workshops, and conferences to public officials on municipal debt and  

[12:1:76,530] public fund investment topics. In addition, the Commission provides technical assistance to public officials and taxpayers  

[12:2:76,540] through direct interaction and public forums to disseminate relevant information.  

[12:3:65,556] • Policy Research - Undertakes original research on the issuance and administration of public debt and on the investment of  

[12:4:76,566] public funds. Research results are published in the form of reports, issue briefs, or articles and are disseminated in printed  

[12:5:76,576] and electronic forms.

[8:0:165,377] 0959   California Debt Limit Allocation Committee  

[8:1:66,399] The California Debt Limit Allocation Committee's mission is to allocate tax-exempt, private activity bond authority for the State  

[8:2:66,409] of California. Private activity bonds may be used by the private sector for projects and programs that provide a public benefit,  

[8:3:66,419] such as the creation of affordable housing.  

[9:0:66,439] The federal government limits the total amount of tax-exempt private activity bond authority that can be issued on an annual  

[9:1:66,450] basis. Except for the Qualified Public Educational Facility Bond Program, the bond authority limit (debt limit) is calculated by  

[9:2:66,460] multiplying the state population by $105. California's limit totaled over $4.1 billion in 2020. (California's limit for the Qualified  

[9:3:66,470] Public Educational Facility Bond Program is calculated separately by multiplying the state population by $10, and totaled $395  

[9:4:66,480] million for 2020.)  

[10:0:66,501] The Committee's allocation of tax-exempt bond authority results in the issuance of bonds by cities, counties, joint powers  

[10:1:66,511] authorities and state agencies. The bonds are purchased and used by the private sector and are not an obligation of the state  

[10:2:66,521] or federal government.  

[11:0:66,541] The Committee administers five active programs that are funded through the allocation and issuance of tax-exempt private  

[11:1:66,552] activity bonds.   The Committee is funded on a fee-supported basis and is comprised of the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the  

[11:2:66,562] Governor, or upon his designation, the Director of Finance, and the State Controller.

[8:0:66,354] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:0:66,374] 0810 - CALIFORNIA DEBT LIMIT ALLOCATION COMMITTEE  

[10:0:66,394] To lower the cost of financing, specified entities can issue various bonds, including mortgage revenue bonds (MRBs) that  

[10:1:66,404] support below-market interest rate mortgage loans; and mortgage credit certificates (MCCs) that reduce a homebuyer's federal  

[10:2:66,414] tax liability. Below is a summary of each program:  

[11:0:66,435] Qualified Residential Rental Project Program - Tax-exempt housing revenue bonds lower the cost for developers of multifamily  

[11:1:66,445] rental housing, to acquire land and construct new housing, or purchase and rehabilitate existing housing. The developers  

[11:2:66,455] produce affordable rental housing for low-income households by reducing rental rates charged to these individuals and  

[11:3:66,465] families. To qualify, developers must elect either to reserve at least 20% of the units for households earning up to 50% AMI or  

[11:4:66,476] reserve at least 40% of the units for households earning up to 60% AMI. Projects that receive an award of bond authority can  

[11:5:66,486] apply for non-competitive four-percent tax credits using the California Debt Limit Allocation Committee/California Tax Credit  

[11:6:66,496] Allocation Committee Joint Application.  

[12:0:66,516] Single-Family Housing Program - Tax-exempt MRBs or MCCs to assist first-time homebuyers with purchasing homes.  

[12:1:66,527] Homebuyers may purchase single-family homes, either freestanding or detached, condominiums, or townhouses. Program  

[12:2:66,537] participants must meet income limits and must purchase a home that falls within the program's purchase price limitations.  

[13:0:66,557] Industrial Development Bond Project Program - Small-Issue industrial development bonds are tax-exempt private activity bonds  

[13:1:66,567] issued to assist manufacturing facilities finance capital expenditures. These bonds offer interest rate savings to small and  

[13:2:66,578] midsize manufacturers in contrast to conventional loans, and help manufacturers retain and create new jobs within their  

[13:3:66,588] communities.  

[14:0:66,608] Exempt Facility Program - Tax-exempt private activity bonds issued to finance any of the following facilities identified by the IRS  

[14:1:66,618] as an exempt facility, including but not limited to: solid waste disposal and waste recycling facilities, mass commuting facilities,  

[14:2:66,629] high-speed rail, energy and power generating facilities, and sustainable design facilities. Loan interest rate savings enable the  

[14:3:66,639] project owners to charge lower customer rates, while assisting communities they serve to meet mandated requirements to  

[14:4:66,649] protect and enhance the environment.  

[15:0:66,669] Qualified Public Educational Facility Bond Program - Tax-exempt private activity bonds issued to finance the construction,  

[15:1:66,680] renovation, and furnishing of primary and secondary school facilities.  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[11:2:66,531] agency representative appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules, and a local agency representative appointed by the

[5:0:66,126] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,145] 0820 - CALIFORNIA TRANSPORTATION FINANCING AUTHORITY  

[7:0:66,166] The Authority was established to assist transportation agencies in obtaining financing to develop transportation projects. To  

[7:1:66,176] meet this objective, statutes allow the Authority to issue, or to approve specified project sponsors to issue revenue bonds to  

[7:2:66,186] fund transportation projects backed in whole or in part, by various revenue streams of transportation funds (including toll  

[7:3:66,196] revenues). Statutes provide the authority to approve the imposition and collection of tolls on proposed transportation projects  

[7:4:66,207] under certain conditions. The planning, programming, and allocation of transportation projects are performed by the California  

[7:5:66,217] Transportation Commission and the California Department of Transportation, as appropriate.  

[8:0:166,254] 0968   California Tax Credit Allocation Committee  

[9:0:66,276] The mission of the California Tax Credit Allocation Committee is to fairly allocate federal and state tax credits to create and  

[9:1:66,286] maintain safe, quality affordable rental housing for low-income households in California. The Committee does this by forming  

[9:2:66,296] partnerships with developers, investors and public entities.  

[10:0:66,316] The Committee assists development of rental housing projects for low-income families and monitors these projects for years  

[10:1:66,327] after they are placed in service to ensure compliance with federal and state tax credit program requirements of the Committee.  

[10:2:66,337] Coordinating with state and local housing fund providers, and with private investors, the Committee helps to create and  

[10:3:66,347] maintain a supply of quality, affordable housing.  

[11:0:66,367] The Committee consists of seven members, including five voting members and two advisors. The voting members are the  

[11:1:66,378] Treasurer (Chairperson of the Committee), the Governor (who may choose the Director of Finance as his or her  

[11:2:66,388] representative), the State Controller, the Director of Housing and Community Development, and the Executive Director of the  

[11:3:66,398] California Housing Finance Agency. The non-voting (advisory) members are two local government representatives. One local  

[11:4:66,408] representative is associated with a city government and appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly. The other is a county  

[11:5:66,418] government representative appointed by the Senate Rules Committee.

[6:0:66,278] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,297] 0840 - CALIFORNIA TAX CREDIT ALLOCATION COMMITTEE  

[7:0:66,317] The Federal Program  

[8:0:66,338] Congress authorized the federal Low-Income Housing Tax Credit (LIHTC) program in 1986. It replaced traditional housing tax  

[8:1:66,348] incentives, such as accelerated depreciation, with a tax credit that enables developers of affordable rental housing to raise  

[8:2:66,358] project equity through the "sale" of tax benefits to investors. The federal per-capita tax credit ceiling is calculated annually and  

[8:3:66,368] indexed for inflation. 

[9:0:66,389] Two types of federal tax credits are available, generally referred to as 9-percent and 4-percent credits. These terms refer to the  

[9:1:66,399] percentage of a project's "qualified basis" an investor in LIHTC projects may deduct from his or her federal income tax liability  

[9:2:66,409] annually in each of ten years. A project's qualified basis is the portion of the total project cost used to calculate the amount of  

[9:3:66,419] the tax credit and typically excludes non-depreciable costs such as the purchase of land. The affordable housing project  

[9:4:66,429] sponsor uses or sells ten times the project's tax-credit allocation amount because investors can take the annual tax credit each  

[9:5:66,440] year for a ten-year period.  

[10:0:66,457] The federal per-capita tax credit ceiling for 9-percent credits is calculated annually and indexed for inflation.   For 2020, each  

[10:1:66,468] state has an annual housing credit ceiling of $2.81 per   state resident.   Additionally, each state may qualify annually for a share  

[10:2:66,478] of unused credits in a national pool.  

[11:0:66,495] Developments financed with tax-exempt bond proceeds may receive the 4% federal tax credit. The sponsors of such projects  

[11:1:66,506] must apply to the Committee and must conform to applicable federal and state statutory and regulatory requirements, but there  

[11:2:66,516] is no annual cap on the amount of credit that may be awarded by the state to such developments.  

[11:3:66,534] Under federal law, credit projects must remain affordable for at least 30 years. However, California's program generally requires  

[11:4:66,544] maintaining affordability for 55 years. Land use agreements are recorded against each credit project to ensure compliance.  

[12:0:66,572] The State LIHTC Program  

[13:0:66,592] In 1987, recognizing the high cost of housing in California, the Legislature authorized the state's program to augment the  

[13:1:66,602] federal program. Housing projects receiving (or that have previously received) an allocation of federal tax credits may apply for  

[13:2:66,612] an allocation of state tax credits. Projects serving farmworkers may apply for state tax credits regardless of their federal tax  

[13:3:66,623] credit status.  

[14:0:66,643] The annual state credit ceiling is indexed for inflation, and for 2020, was $102.7 million. Investors take the state tax credit  

[14:1:66,653] annually over a four-year period in contrast to the ten-year federal period.  

[15:0:66,671] Chapter 159, Statutes of 2019, authorized the California Tax Credit Allocation Committee and the California Debt Limit  

[15:1:66,681] Allocation Committee to   issue an additional $500 million in state tax credits in 2020 to be paired with the 4% federal program to  

[15:2:66,691] bolster new construction of low income housing. Per AB 83, this $500 million tax credit will be issued in 2021 pursuant to an  

[15:3:66,702] authorization in the   annual Budget Act or related legislation.  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,69] Farmworker Housing Program  

[4:0:66,89] Chapter 521, Statutes of 2008, folded the previous Farmworker Housing Assistance Tax Credit program into the general state  

[4:1:66,99] LIHTC program as a $500,000 annual set-aside in support of farmworker housing. Pursuant to Chapter 372, Statutes of 2017,  

[4:2:66,109] these credits differ from other state credits in that the credit percentage for tax-exempt bond financed projects is higher and  

[4:3:66,120] projects may receive state credits even if they receive a federal tax credit basis increase.

[2:0:88,32] 0971   California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing 

[2:1:244,47] Authority - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing Authority was established by Chapter 908, Statutes  

[3:1:66,79] of 1980, to promote the prompt and efficient development of energy sources which are renewable or which more efficiently  

[3:2:66,89] utilize and conserve scarce energy resources. Recognizing the importance of developing a secure energy future to protect the  

[3:3:66,99] environment and ensure economic stability, the Authority advances the state's goals of reducing greenhouse gas emissions by  

[3:4:66,109] providing financing options to assist industries in increasing the deployment of sustainable and renewable energy sources,  

[3:5:66,120] implementing measures that increase the efficiency of the use of energy, creating high quality employment opportunities, and  

[3:6:66,130] lessening the state's dependence on fossil fuels. To support these goals, the Authority provides financing and credit  

[3:7:66,140] enhancements to promote the establishment of facilities that use alternative methods and sources of energy, and facilities  

[3:8:66,150] needed for the development and commercialization of advanced transportation technologies.  

[4:0:66,171] The Authority consists of five members: the State Treasurer, who serves as the chairperson, the State Controller, the Director  

[4:1:66,181] of the Department of Finance, the Chairperson of the State Energy Resources Conservation and Development Commission,  

[4:2:66,191] and the President of the Public Utilities Commission.

[3:0:66,69] Financial assistance can take the form of loans, loan loss reserves, interest rate reductions, proceeds of bonds issued by the  

[3:1:66,79] Authority,   loan guarantees or other credit enhancements, contributions of money, or a combination thereof, as determined and  

[3:2:66,89] approved by resolution of the Authority.  

[4:0:66,107] The Authority is a conduit issuer of tax-exempt private activity bonds to finance local district heating or cooling facilities, and  

[4:1:66,117] private activity bonds for 501(c)(3) non-profits. Past issuances total more than $212 million in bond financing for green projects  

[4:2:66,127] in California.  

[5:0:66,148] In 2010, the Authority launched a sales and use tax exclusion (STE) program for advanced transportation and alternative  

[5:1:66,158] source manufacturing in California (Chapter 10, Statutes of 2010). The STE program   expanded   (Chapter 677, Statutes of  

[5:2:66,168] 2012)   to include advanced manufacturing, with an annual cap of $100 million available for STE awards. Chapter 768, Statutes  

[5:3:66,178] of 2015, further expanded the program to also include equipment primarily used to process recycled feedstock and equipment  

[5:4:66,188] that primarily utilizes recycled feedstock in the production of another product.   In 2019, Chapter 690, Statutes of 2019, extended  

[5:5:66,199] the STE program sunset date to January 1, 2026, and Chapter 672, Statutes of 2019, expanded the job creation-related criteria  

[5:6:66,209] by which CAEATFA must evaluate applications. The objective of this program is to promote the creation of California-based  

[5:7:66,219] manufacturing, businesses, and jobs that are aimed at reducing greenhouse gases, air and water pollution, and energy  

[5:8:66,229] consumption.  

[6:0:66,250] Legislation in 2010 (Chapter 15, Statutes of 2010), 2011 (Chapter 9, Statutes of 2011, First Extraordinary Session), and 2013  

[6:1:66,260] (Chapter 356, Statutes of 2013), authorized financial assistance to encourage energy efficiency retrofits. The Authority  

[6:2:66,270] developed a loan loss reserve program   for residential whole house energy efficiency and renewable energy projects, and   a risk  

[6:3:66,280] mitigation program for residential Property Assessed Clean Energy programs in California. Programs to support low-interest  

[6:4:66,290] financing of Property Assessed Clean Energy efficiency projects in commercial buildings are in discussion.  

[7:0:66,311] The Budget Act of 2014 authorized administration of the California Hub for Energy Efficiency Financing on behalf of, and in  

[7:1:66,321] collaboration with, the California Public Utilities Commission   to develop and launch energy efficiency financing pilot programs   to  

[7:2:66,331] encourage and leverage private capital lending   (in both the residential and commercial sectors). These programs   employ  

[7:3:66,341] various types of credit enhancements, lower costs and expand access to capital for Californians making   energy efficiency  

[7:4:66,352] improvements   to help achieve the state's   energy efficiency and decarbonization   goals. The residential pilot, launched in 2016,  

[7:5:66,362] has now transitioned to a full program.

[14:3:66,713] Exempt Bond Program. Over the last twenty-six years, the Authority has evolved to provide financing assistance to California's
